      <p>
       <b>
        Heathrow Airport
       </b>
       (also known as
       <b>
        London Heathrow
       </b>
       )
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association_airport_code" title="International Air Transport Association airport code">
        IATA
       </a>
       :
       <b>
        LHR
       </b>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Civil_Aviation_Organization_airport_code" title="International Civil Aviation Organization airport code">
        ICAO
       </a>
       :
       <b>
        EGLL
       </b>
       ) is a major
       <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">
        international airport
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">
        London
       </a>
       , United Kingdom. Heathrow is the
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_busiest_airports_by_international_passenger_traffic" title="List of busiest airports by international passenger traffic">
        second busiest airport in the world
       </a>
       by international passenger traffic (surpassed by
       <a href="/wiki/Dubai_International_Airport" title="Dubai International Airport">
        Dubai International
       </a>
       in 2014), as well as the
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Europe" title="List of the busiest airports in Europe">
        busiest airport in Europe by passenger traffic
       </a>
       , and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" title="World's busiest airports by passenger traffic">
        seventh busiest airport in the world
       </a>
       by total passenger traffic. In 2016, it handled a record 75.7 million passengers, a 1.0% increase from 2015.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stats_1-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-stats-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Heathrow lies 14
       <a href="/wiki/Mile" title="Mile">
        miles
       </a>
       (23 km) west of
       <a href="/wiki/Central_London" title="Central London">
        Central London
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aip_3-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-aip-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and has two parallel east–west
       <a href="/wiki/Runway" title="Runway">
        runways
       </a>
       along with four operational
       <a href="/wiki/Airport_terminal" title="Airport terminal">
        terminals
       </a>
       on a site that covers 12.27 square kilometres (4.74 sq mi). The airport is owned and operated by
       <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport_Holdings" title="Heathrow Airport Holdings">
        Heathrow Airport Holdings
       </a>
       , which itself is owned by FGP TopCo Limited, an international consortium led by
       <a href="/wiki/Ferrovial" title="Ferrovial">
        Ferrovial
       </a>
       that also includes
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qatar_Holding_LLC" title="Qatar Holding LLC">
        Qatar Holding LLC
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Caisse_de_d%C3%A9p%C3%B4t_et_placement_du_Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Caisse de dépôt et placement du Québec">
        Caisse de dépôt et placement du Québec
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/GIC_Private_Limited" title="GIC Private Limited">
        GIC Private Limited
       </a>
       , Alinda Capital Partners,
       <a href="/wiki/China_Investment_Corporation" title="China Investment Corporation">
        China Investment Corporation
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Universities_Superannuation_Scheme" title="Universities Superannuation Scheme">
        Universities Superannuation Scheme
       </a>
       (USS).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       London Heathrow is the primary hub for
       <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">
        British Airways
       </a>
       and the primary operating base for
       <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Atlantic" title="Virgin Atlantic">
        Virgin Atlantic
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In September 2012, the
       <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Government of the United Kingdom">
        UK government
       </a>
       established the
       <a href="/wiki/Airports_Commission" title="Airports Commission">
        Airports Commission
       </a>
       , an independent commission chaired by
       <a href="/wiki/Howard_Davies_(economist)" title="Howard Davies (economist)">
        Sir Howard Davies
       </a>
       to examine various options for increasing capacity at
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_the_United_Kingdom_and_the_British_Crown_Dependencies" title="List of airports in the United Kingdom and the British Crown Dependencies">
        UK airports
       </a>
       . In July 2015, the commission backed a third runway at Heathrow, which the government approved in October 2016.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Location">
        Location
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Location">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Qantas_b747_over_houses_arp.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1095" data-file-width="1533" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Qantas_b747_over_houses_arp.jpg/220px-Qantas_b747_over_houses_arp.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Qantas_b747_over_houses_arp.jpg/330px-Qantas_b747_over_houses_arp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Qantas_b747_over_houses_arp.jpg/440px-Qantas_b747_over_houses_arp.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Qantas_b747_over_houses_arp.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A
         <a href="/wiki/Qantas" title="Qantas">
          Qantas
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-400" title="Boeing 747-400">
          Boeing 747-400
         </a>
         on approach to London Heathrow 27L runway.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
          <a href="#cite_note-8">
           [8]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Heathrow is 14 mi (23 km) west of central London,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aip_3-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-aip-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       near the south end of the
       <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Hillingdon" title="London Borough of Hillingdon">
        London Borough of Hillingdon
       </a>
       on a parcel of land that is designated part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Green_Belt" title="Metropolitan Green Belt">
        Metropolitan Green Belt
       </a>
       . The airport is surrounded by the villages of
       <a href="/wiki/Harlington,_London" title="Harlington, London">
        Harlington
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Harmondsworth" title="Harmondsworth">
        Harmondsworth
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Longford,_London" title="Longford, London">
        Longford
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Cranford,_London" title="Cranford, London">
        Cranford
       </a>
       to the north and by
       <a href="/wiki/Hounslow" title="Hounslow">
        Hounslow
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Hatton,_London" title="Hatton, London">
        Hatton
       </a>
       to the east. To the south lie
       <a href="/wiki/Bedfont" title="Bedfont">
        Bedfont
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Stanwell" title="Stanwell">
        Stanwell
       </a>
       while to the west Heathrow is separated from
       <a href="/wiki/Slough" title="Slough">
        Slough
       </a>
       in Berkshire by the
       <a href="/wiki/M25_motorway" title="M25 motorway">
        M25 motorway
       </a>
       . Heathrow falls entirely under the
       <a href="/wiki/TW_postcode_area" title="TW postcode area">
        TW postcode area
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       As the airport is located west of London and as its runways run east–west, an airliner's landing approach is usually directly over the conurbation of London when the wind is from the west.
      </p>
      <p>
       Along with
       <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">
        Gatwick
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/London_Stansted_Airport" title="London Stansted Airport">
        Stansted
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Luton_Airport" title="Luton Airport">
        Luton
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/London_Southend_Airport" title="London Southend Airport">
        Southend
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/London_City_Airport" title="London City Airport">
        London City
       </a>
       , Heathrow is one of six airports with scheduled services serving the London area, although only Heathrow and London City are within
       <a href="/wiki/Greater_London" title="Greater London">
        Greater London
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div style="clear:left;">
      </div>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aerial_photograph_of_Heathrow_Airport,_1955.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="629" data-file-width="800" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Aerial_photograph_of_Heathrow_Airport%2C_1955.jpg/220px-Aerial_photograph_of_Heathrow_Airport%2C_1955.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Aerial_photograph_of_Heathrow_Airport%2C_1955.jpg/330px-Aerial_photograph_of_Heathrow_Airport%2C_1955.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Aerial_photograph_of_Heathrow_Airport%2C_1955.jpg/440px-Aerial_photograph_of_Heathrow_Airport%2C_1955.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aerial_photograph_of_Heathrow_Airport,_1955.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Aerial photo of Heathrow Airport from the 1950s, before the terminals were built
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         For a chronicled history of Heathrow Airport, see
         <a href="/wiki/History_of_Heathrow_Airport" title="History of Heathrow Airport">
          History of Heathrow Airport
         </a>
         .
        </i>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       Heathrow Airport originated in 1929 as a small airfield (
       <a href="/wiki/Great_West_Aerodrome" title="Great West Aerodrome">
        Great West Aerodrome
       </a>
       ) on land south-east of the hamlet of
       <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_(hamlet)" title="Heathrow (hamlet)">
        Heathrow
       </a>
       from which the airport takes its name. At that time there were farms,
       <a href="/wiki/Market_garden" title="Market garden">
        market gardens
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Orchard" title="Orchard">
        orchards
       </a>
       there: there was a "Heathrow Farm" about where Terminal 1 is now, a "Heathrow Hall" and a "Heathrow House". This hamlet was largely along a country lane (Heathrow Road) which ran roughly along the east and south edges of the present central terminals area.
      </p>
      <p>
       Development of the whole Heathrow area as a very much larger airport began in 1944: it was stated to be for long-distance military aircraft bound for the Far East. But by the time the airfield was nearing completion,
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
        World War II
       </a>
       had ended. The government continued to develop the airport as a civil airport; it opened as London Airport in 1946 and was renamed Heathrow Airport in 1966. The masterplan
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (January 2017)">
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       for the airport was designed by Sir Frederick Gibberd, who designed the original terminals and central area buildings, including the original control tower and the multi-faith chapel of St George's.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">
        Operations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Operations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Facilities">
        Facilities
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Facilities">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TerminalFiveAirportHeathrowAugust2012.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3240" data-file-width="4320" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/TerminalFiveAirportHeathrowAugust2012.JPG/220px-TerminalFiveAirportHeathrowAugust2012.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/TerminalFiveAirportHeathrowAugust2012.JPG/330px-TerminalFiveAirportHeathrowAugust2012.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/TerminalFiveAirportHeathrowAugust2012.JPG/440px-TerminalFiveAirportHeathrowAugust2012.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TerminalFiveAirportHeathrowAugust2012.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Central waiting area in
         <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Terminal_5" title="Heathrow Terminal 5">
          Terminal 5
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Concorde_g-boab_in_storage_arp.jpg">

        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Concorde_g-boab_in_storage_arp.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Concorde" title="Concorde">
          Concorde
         </a>
         G-BOAB in storage at Heathrow
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Four_aircraft_on_the_approach_to_LHR_runway_09L_10Sep2015_arp.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3230" data-file-width="4246" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Four_aircraft_on_the_approach_to_LHR_runway_09L_10Sep2015_arp.jpg/220px-Four_aircraft_on_the_approach_to_LHR_runway_09L_10Sep2015_arp.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Four_aircraft_on_the_approach_to_LHR_runway_09L_10Sep2015_arp.jpg/330px-Four_aircraft_on_the_approach_to_LHR_runway_09L_10Sep2015_arp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Four_aircraft_on_the_approach_to_LHR_runway_09L_10Sep2015_arp.jpg/440px-Four_aircraft_on_the_approach_to_LHR_runway_09L_10Sep2015_arp.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Four_aircraft_on_the_approach_to_LHR_runway_09L_10Sep2015_arp.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Four aircraft on the approach to Heathrow runway 09L
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:London_Heathrow_tower_and_Virgin_B747_(5048342074)_(2).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="682" data-file-width="1024" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/London_Heathrow_tower_and_Virgin_B747_%285048342074%29_%282%29.jpg/220px-London_Heathrow_tower_and_Virgin_B747_%285048342074%29_%282%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/London_Heathrow_tower_and_Virgin_B747_%285048342074%29_%282%29.jpg/330px-London_Heathrow_tower_and_Virgin_B747_%285048342074%29_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/London_Heathrow_tower_and_Virgin_B747_%285048342074%29_%282%29.jpg/440px-London_Heathrow_tower_and_Virgin_B747_%285048342074%29_%282%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">

         </div>
         Heathrow's control tower
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Heathrow_Terminal_5C_Iwelumo-1.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="797" data-file-width="1200" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Heathrow_Terminal_5C_Iwelumo-1.jpg/220px-Heathrow_Terminal_5C_Iwelumo-1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Heathrow_Terminal_5C_Iwelumo-1.jpg/330px-Heathrow_Terminal_5C_Iwelumo-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Heathrow_Terminal_5C_Iwelumo-1.jpg/440px-Heathrow_Terminal_5C_Iwelumo-1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Heathrow_Terminal_5C_Iwelumo-1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         British Airways aircraft at
         <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Terminal_5" title="Heathrow Terminal 5">
          Terminal 5C
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Heathrow Airport is used by over 80 airlines flying to 185 destinations in 84 countries. The airport is the primary
       <a href="/wiki/Airline_hub" title="Airline hub">
        hub
       </a>
       of British Airways and is a base for
       <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Atlantic" title="Virgin Atlantic">
        Virgin Atlantic
       </a>
       . It has four passenger terminals (numbered 2 to 5) and a cargo terminal. Of Heathrow's 73.4 million passengers in 2014, 93% were international travellers; the remaining 7% were bound for (or arriving from) places in the UK.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Facts_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Facts-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The busiest single destination in passenger numbers is New York, with over 3 million passengers flying between Heathrow and JFK Airport in 2013.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 1950s, Heathrow had six runways, arranged in three pairs at different angles in the shape of a
       <a href="/wiki/Hexagram" title="Hexagram">
        hexagram
       </a>
       (
       <big>
        ✡
       </big>
       ) with the permanent passenger terminal in the middle and the older terminal along the north edge of the field; two of its runways would always be within 30° of the wind direction. As the required length for runways has grown, Heathrow now has only two parallel runways running east–west. These are extended versions of the two east–west runways from the original hexagram. From the air, almost all of the original runways can still be seen, incorporated into the present system of taxiways. North of the northern runway and the former taxiway and aprons, now the site of extensive car parks, is the entrance to the access tunnel and the site of Heathrow's unofficial "
       <a href="/wiki/Gate_guardian" title="Gate guardian">
        gate guardian
       </a>
       ". For many years the home of a 40% scale model of a British Airways
       <a href="/wiki/Concorde" title="Concorde">
        Concorde
       </a>
       , G-CONC, the site has been occupied by a model of an Emirates
       <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">
        Airbus A380
       </a>
       since 2008.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Heathrow Airport has
       <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">
        Anglican
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">
        Catholic
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nonconformist" title="Nonconformist">
        Free Church
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">
        Hindu
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish" title="Jewish">
        Jewish
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">
        Muslim
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">
        Sikh
       </a>
       chaplains. There is a
       <a href="/wiki/Multifaith_space" title="Multifaith space">
        multi-faith prayer room
       </a>
       and counselling room in each terminal, in addition to
       <a href="/wiki/St_George%27s_Interdenominational_Chapel,_Heathrow_Airport" title="St George's Interdenominational Chapel, Heathrow Airport">
        St. George's Interdenominational Chapel
       </a>
       in an underground vault adjacent to the old control tower, where Christian services take place. The chaplains organize and lead prayers at certain times in the prayer room.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The airport has its own resident press corps, consisting of six photographers and one TV crew, serving all the major newspapers and television stations around the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_n_13-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ref_n-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Most of Heathrow's internal roads are initial letter coded by area: N in the north (e.g. Newall Road), E in the east (e.g. Elmdon Road), S in the south (e.g. Stratford Road), W in the west (e.g. Walrus Road), C in the centre (e.g. Camborne Road).
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Flight_movements">
        Flight movements
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Flight movements">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Aircraft destined for Heathrow are usually routed over one of four main reporting points:
       <a href="/wiki/Bovingdon_stack" title="Bovingdon stack">
        Bovingdon
       </a>
       <i>
        (BNN)
       </i>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Hertfordshire" title="Hertfordshire">
        Hertfordshire
       </a>
       , Lambourne
       <i>
        (LAM)
       </i>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Essex" title="Essex">
        Essex
       </a>
       , Biggin Hill
       <i>
        (BIG)
       </i>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Bromley" title="Bromley">
        Bromley
       </a>
       and Ockham
       <i>
        (OCK)
       </i>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Surrey" title="Surrey">
        Surrey
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_2008a_14-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ref_2008a-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Each is defined by a
       <a href="/wiki/VHF_omnidirectional_range" title="VHF omnidirectional range">
        VOR
       </a>
       radio-navigational beacon. When the airport is busy, aircraft orbit in the associated
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holding_(aviation)" title="Holding (aviation)">
        hold
       </a>
       patterns. These holding areas lie to the northwest, northeast, southeast and southwest of the London conurbation. Aircraft hold between 7,000 feet and 15,000 feet at 1,000 foot intervals. If these holds become full, aircraft are held at more distant points before being cleared onward to one of the four main holds.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Air_traffic_controller" title="Air traffic controller">
        Air traffic controllers
       </a>
       at Heathrow Approach Control (based in
       <a href="/wiki/Swanwick,_Hampshire" title="Swanwick, Hampshire">
        Swanwick, Hampshire
       </a>
       ) then guide the aircraft to their final approach, merging aircraft from the four holds into a single stream of traffic, sometimes as close as 2.5 nautical miles (4.6 km; 2.9 mi) apart. Considerable use is made of
       <a href="/wiki/Continuous_descent_approach" title="Continuous descent approach">
        continuous descent approach
       </a>
       techniques to minimize the environmental effects of incoming aircraft, particularly at night.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heathrow2004_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Heathrow2004-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Once an aircraft is established on its final approach, control is handed over to Heathrow Tower.
      </p>
      <p>
       When runway alternation was introduced, aircraft generated significantly more noise on departure than when landing, so a preference for westerly operations during daylight was introduced, which continues to this day.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_o_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ref_o-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In this mode, aircraft depart towards the west and approach from the east over London, thereby minimizing the impact of noise on the most densely populated areas. Heathrow's two runways generally operate in segregated mode, whereby arriving aircraft are allocated to one runway and departing aircraft to the other. To further reduce noise nuisance to people beneath the approach and departure routes, the use of runways 27R and 27L is swapped at 15:00 each day if the wind is from the west. When landings are easterly there is no alternation; 09L remains the landing runway and 09R the departure runway due to the legacy of the now rescinded
       <a href="/wiki/Cranford_Agreement" title="Cranford Agreement">
        Cranford Agreement
       </a>
       , pending taxiway works to allow the roles to be reversed. Occasionally, landings are allowed on the nominated departure runway, to help reduce airborne delays and to position landing aircraft closer to their terminal, reducing taxi times.
      </p>
      <p>
       Night-time flights at Heathrow are subject to
       <a href="/wiki/Night_flying_restrictions" title="Night flying restrictions">
        restrictions
       </a>
       . Between 23:00 and 04:00, the noisiest aircraft (rated
       <a href="/wiki/Quota_Count_system" title="Quota Count system">
        QC
       </a>
       /8 and QC/16) cannot be scheduled for operation. In addition, during the night quota period (23:30–06:00) there are four limits:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        A limit on the number of flights allowed;
       </li>
       <li>
        A
        <a href="/wiki/Quota_Count_system" title="Quota Count system">
         Quota Count system
        </a>
        which limits the total amount of noise permitted, but allows operators to choose to operate fewer noisy aircraft or a greater number of quieter planes;
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_p_17-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Ref_p-17">
          [17]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        QC/4 aircraft cannot be scheduled for operation.
       </li>
       <li>
        A voluntary agreement with the airlines that no early morning arrivals will be scheduled to land before 04:30.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       A trial of "noise relief zones" ran from December 2012 to March 2013, which concentrated approach flight paths into defined areas compared with the existing paths which were spread out. The zones used alternated weekly, meaning residents in the "no-fly" areas received respite from aircraft noise for set periods.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, it was concluded that some residents in other areas experienced a significant disbenefit as a result of the trial and that it should therefore not be taken forward in its current form. Heathrow received more than 25,000 noise complaints in just three months over the summer of 2016, but around half were made by the same ten people.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Regulation">
        Regulation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Regulation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Landing_slot" title="Landing slot">
        Landing slot
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Until it was required to sell Gatwick and Stansted Airports, Heathrow Airport Holdings held a dominant position in the London aviation market, and has been heavily regulated by the Civil Aviation Authority (CAA) as to how much it can charge airlines to land. The annual increase in
       <a href="/wiki/Landing_fee" title="Landing fee">
        landing charge
       </a>
       per passenger was capped at inflation minus 3% until 1 April 2003. From 2003 to 2007 charges increased by inflation plus 6.5% per year, taking the fee to £9.28 per passenger in 2007. In March 2008, the CAA announced that the charge would be allowed to increase by 23.5% to £12.80 from 1 April 2008 and by inflation plus 7.5% for each of the following four years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_r_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ref_r-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In April 2013, the CAA announced a proposal for Heathrow to charge fees calculated by inflation minus 1.3%, continuing until 2019.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Whilst the cost of landing at Heathrow is determined by the CAA and Heathrow Airport Holdings, the allocation of
       <a href="/wiki/Landing_slot" title="Landing slot">
        landing slots
       </a>
       to airlines is carried out by Airport Co-ordination Limited (ACL).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Until 2008, air traffic between Heathrow and the United States was strictly governed by the countries' bilateral
       <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_II_Agreement" title="Bermuda II Agreement">
        Bermuda II
       </a>
       treaty. The treaty originally allowed only British Airways,
       <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_World_Airways" title="Pan American World Airways">
        Pan Am
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Trans_World_Airlines" title="Trans World Airlines">
        TWA
       </a>
       to fly from Heathrow to the US. In 1991, PAA and TWA sold their rights to
       <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">
        United Airlines
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">
        American Airlines
       </a>
       respectively, while Virgin Atlantic was added to the list of airlines allowed to operate on these routes. The Bermuda bilateral agreement conflicted with the Right of Establishment of the United Kingdom in relation to its EU membership, and as a consequence the UK was ordered to drop the agreement in 2004. A new "
       <a href="/wiki/EU%E2%80%93US_Open_Skies_Agreement" title="EU–US Open Skies Agreement">
        open skies
       </a>
       " agreement was signed by the United States and the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
        European Union
       </a>
       on 30 April 2007 and came into effect on 30 March 2008. Shortly afterwards, additional US airlines, including
       <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Airlines" title="Northwest Airlines">
        Northwest Airlines
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Continental_Airlines" title="Continental Airlines">
        Continental Airlines
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/US_Airways" title="US Airways">
        US Airways
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">
        Delta Air Lines
       </a>
       started services to Heathrow.
      </p>
      <p>
       The airport has been criticized in recent years for overcrowding and delays;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_2007_23-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ref_2007-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       according to Heathrow Airport Holdings, Heathrow's facilities were originally designed to accommodate 55 million passengers annually. The number of passengers using the airport reached a record 70 million in 2012.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2007 the airport was voted the world's least favorite, alongside
       <a href="/wiki/O%27Hare_International_Airport" title="O'Hare International Airport">
        Chicago O'Hare
       </a>
       , in a
       <a href="/wiki/TripAdvisor" title="TripAdvisor">
        TripAdvisor
       </a>
       survey.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Millward2007_25-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Millward2007-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, the opening of Terminal 5 in 2008 has relieved some pressure on terminal facilities, increasing the airport's terminal capacity to 90 million passengers per year. A tie-up is also in place with McLaren Applied Technologies to optimize the general procedure, reducing delays and pollution.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       With only two runways, operating at over 98% of their capacity, Heathrow has little room for more flights, although the increasing use of larger aircraft such as the Airbus A380 will allow some increase in passenger numbers. It is difficult for existing airlines to obtain landing slots to enable them to increase their services from the airport, or for new airlines to start operations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Airport2002_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Airport2002-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       To increase the number of flights, Heathrow Airport Holdings has proposed using the existing two runways in 'mixed mode' whereby aircraft would be allowed to take off and land on the same runway. This would increase the airport's capacity from its current 480,000 movements per year to as many as 550,000 according to British Airways CEO
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Willie_Walsh_(Irish_businessman)" title="Willie Walsh (Irish businessman)">
        Willie Walsh
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_t_28-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ref_t-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Heathrow Airport Holdings has also proposed building a third runway to the north of the airport, which would significantly increase traffic capacity (see
       <a href="#Future_expansion_and_plans">
        Future expansion
       </a>
       below).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Webster2007_29-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Webster2007-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Security">
        Security
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Security">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Policing of the airport is the responsibility of the
       <a href="/wiki/Aviation_Security_Operational_Command_Unit" title="Aviation Security Operational Command Unit">
        aviation security
       </a>
       unit of the
       <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Police_Service" title="Metropolitan Police Service">
        Metropolitan Police
       </a>
       , although
       <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">
        the army
       </a>
       , including armored vehicles of the
       <a href="/wiki/Household_Cavalry" title="Household Cavalry">
        Household Cavalry
       </a>
       , has occasionally been deployed at the airport during periods of heightened security.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Full_body_scanner" title="Full body scanner">
        Full body scanners
       </a>
       are now used at the airport, and passengers who object to their use after being selected are required to submit to a hand search in a private room.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scanners_30-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-scanners-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The scanners display passengers' bodies as a cartoon-style figure, with indicators showing where concealed items may be.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scanners_30-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-scanners-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The new imagery was introduced initially as a trial in September 2011 following complaints over privacy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Terminals">
        Terminals
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Terminals">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The airport has 4 terminals. Terminal 2, the newest terminal formerly served
       <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Atlantic_Little_Red" title="Virgin Atlantic Little Red">
        Virgin Atlantic Little Red
       </a>
       and now houses
       <a href="/wiki/Star_Alliance" title="Star Alliance">
        Star Alliance
       </a>
       members along with
       <a href="/wiki/Aer_Lingus" title="Aer Lingus">
        Aer Lingus
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Eurowings" title="Eurowings">
        Eurowings
       </a>
       , the new
       <a href="/wiki/Flybe" title="Flybe">
        Flybe
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Icelandair" title="Icelandair">
        Icelandair
       </a>
       . Terminal 3 houses
       <a href="/wiki/Oneworld" title="Oneworld">
        Oneworld
       </a>
       members,
       <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Atlantic" title="Virgin Atlantic">
        Virgin Atlantic
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">
        Delta Air Lines
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Garuda_Indonesia" title="Garuda Indonesia">
        Garuda Indonesia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_East_Airlines" title="Middle East Airlines">
        Middle East Airlines
       </a>
       , and few other unaffiliated members with the exception of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iberia" title="Iberia">
        Iberia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Malaysia_Airlines" title="Malaysia Airlines">
        Malaysia Airlines
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Airways" title="Qatar Airways">
        Qatar Airways
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Capital_Airlines" title="Beijing Capital Airlines">
        Beijing Capital Airlines
       </a>
       , the newest airline also operates from Terminal 3. Terminal 4 serves
       <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">
        SkyTeam
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Malaysia_Airlines" title="Malaysia Airlines">
        Malaysia Airlines
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Airways" title="Qatar Airways">
        Qatar Airways
       </a>
       , and most unaffiliated members. Terminal 5 houses the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Airlines_Group" title="International Airlines Group">
        International Airlines Group
       </a>
       -
       <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">
        British Airways
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iberia" title="Iberia">
        Iberia
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Terminal_1_.28Closed.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_1_(Closed)">
        Terminal 1
        <i>
         (Closed)
        </i>
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Terminal 1 (Closed)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Terminal_1" title="Heathrow Terminal 1">
        Heathrow Terminal 1
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Terminal 1 opened in 1968 and was inaugurated by
       <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">
        Queen Elizabeth II
       </a>
       in April 1969.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_w_33-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ref_w-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Before Terminal 5 opened, Terminal 1 was the Heathrow base for British Airways' (BA) domestic and European network and for a few of its long haul routes. The acquisition of
       <a href="/wiki/British_Midland_International" title="British Midland International">
        British Midland International
       </a>
       (BMI) in 2012 by BA's owner
       <a href="/wiki/International_Airlines_Group" title="International Airlines Group">
        International Airlines Group
       </a>
       meant British Airways took over BMI's short-haul and medium-haul destinations from the terminal.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Terminal 1 was also the main base for
       <a href="/wiki/Star_Alliance" title="Star Alliance">
        Star Alliance
       </a>
       members.
      </p>
      <p>
       Terminal 1 closed in June 2015. Its site is being used for an extension to Terminal 2,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which opened in June 2014. A number of newer boarding gates used by Terminal 1 had been built as part of the Terminal 2 development and are being retained as part of Terminal 2.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       British Airways was the last operator in Terminal 1. Two flights of this carrier, one departing to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hannover" title="Hannover">
        Hannover
       </a>
       and one arriving from
       <a href="/wiki/Baku" title="Baku">
        Baku
       </a>
       , marked the terminal closure on 29 June 2015. British Airways operations have been relocated to Terminals 3 and 5.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heathrow_shuts_doors_on_Terminal_1_flights_38-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Heathrow_shuts_doors_on_Terminal_1_flights-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_2">
        Terminal 2
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Terminal 2">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Heathrow_T2_central_overview.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Heathrow_T2_central_overview.jpg/220px-Heathrow_T2_central_overview.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Heathrow_T2_central_overview.jpg/330px-Heathrow_T2_central_overview.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Heathrow_T2_central_overview.jpg/440px-Heathrow_T2_central_overview.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Heathrow_T2_central_overview.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Terminal_2" title="Heathrow Terminal 2">
          Terminal 2
         </a>
         central departures area
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Terminal_2" title="Heathrow Terminal 2">
        Heathrow Terminal 2
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The airport's newest terminal, officially known as the Queen's Terminal, was opened on 4 June 2014.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Designed by Spanish architect
       <a href="/wiki/Luis_Vidal" title="Luis Vidal">
        Luis Vidal
       </a>
       , it was built on the site that had been occupied by the original Terminal 2 and the Queens Building.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBCT2open_41-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-BBCT2open-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The main complex was completed in November 2013 and underwent six months of testing before opening to passengers. It includes a satellite pier (T2B), a 1,340-space car park, an energy center
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (December 2016)">
           clarification needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       and a cooling station to generate chilled water. There are 52 shops and 17 bars and restaurants.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Terminal 2 is used by all
       <a href="/wiki/Star_Alliance" title="Star Alliance">
        Star Alliance
       </a>
       members which fly from Heathrow (consolidating the airlines under Star Alliance's co-location policy "Move Under One Roof").
       <a href="/wiki/Aer_Lingus" title="Aer Lingus">
        Aer Lingus
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Eurowings" title="Eurowings">
        Eurowings
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Flybe" title="Flybe">
        Flybe
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Icelandair" title="Icelandair">
        Icelandair
       </a>
       also operate from the terminal. The airlines moved from their original locations over a six-month period, with only 10% of flights operating from there in the first six weeks (
       <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">
        United Airlines
       </a>
       ' transatlantic flights) to avoid the opening problems seen at Terminal 5.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Development will continue at the terminal to increase capacity in preparation for the closure of Terminal 3 in 2019.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-itv.com_45-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-itv.com-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The original Terminal 2 opened as the Europa Building in 1955 and was the airport's oldest terminal. It had an area of 49,654 m
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (534,470 sq ft) and was designed to handle around 1.2 million passengers annually. In its final years it accommodated up to 8 million. A total of 316 million passengers passed through the terminal in its lifetime. The building was demolished in 2010, along with the
       <a href="/wiki/Queens_Building,_Heathrow" title="Queens Building, Heathrow">
        Queens Building
       </a>
       which had housed airline company offices.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_3">
        Terminal 3
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Terminal 3">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Heathrow_Airport_010.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Heathrow_Airport_010.jpg/220px-Heathrow_Airport_010.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Heathrow_Airport_010.jpg/330px-Heathrow_Airport_010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Heathrow_Airport_010.jpg/440px-Heathrow_Airport_010.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Heathrow_Airport_010.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Terminal_3" title="Heathrow Terminal 3">
          Terminal 3
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Bird%27s-eye_view" title="Bird's-eye view">
          bird's-eye view
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Terminal_3" title="Heathrow Terminal 3">
        Heathrow Terminal 3
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Terminal 3 opened as the Oceanic Terminal on 13 November 1961 to handle flight departures for long-haul routes for foreign carriers to the United States, Asia and other Far Eastern destinations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BAA_History_47-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-BAA_History-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       At this time the airport had a direct helicopter service to Central London from the gardens on the roof of the terminal building. Renamed Terminal 3 in 1968, it was expanded in 1970 with the addition of an arrivals building. Other facilities added included the UK's first
       <a href="/wiki/Moving_walkway" title="Moving walkway">
        moving walkways
       </a>
       . In 2006, the new £105 million Pier 6 was completed
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nqaheu_48-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-nqaheu-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       to accommodate the
       <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">
        Airbus A380
       </a>
       superjumbo;
       <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">
        Emirates
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Qantas" title="Qantas">
        Qantas
       </a>
       operate regular flights from Terminal 3 using the Airbus A380.
      </p>
      <p>
       Redevelopment of Terminal 3's forecourt by the addition of a new four-lane drop-off area and a large pedestrianised plaza, complete with canopy to the front of the terminal building, was completed in 2007. These improvements were intended to improve passengers' experience, reduce traffic congestion and improve security.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_y_49-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ref_y-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As part of this project,
       <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Atlantic" title="Virgin Atlantic">
        Virgin Atlantic
       </a>
       was assigned its own dedicated check-in area, known as 'Zone A', which features a large sculpture and atrium.
      </p>
      <p>
       As of 2013
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , Terminal 3 has an area of 98,962 m
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (1,065,220 sq ft) and in 2011 it handled 19.8 million passengers on 104,100 flights.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Terminal 3 is home to
       <a href="/wiki/Oneworld" title="Oneworld">
        Oneworld
       </a>
       members with the exception of
       <a href="/wiki/Iberia_(airline)" title="Iberia (airline)">
        Iberia
       </a>
       , which uses Terminal 5,
       <a href="/wiki/Malaysia_Airlines" title="Malaysia Airlines">
        Malaysia Airlines
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Airways" title="Qatar Airways">
        Qatar Airways
       </a>
       which use Terminal 4, Skyteam members Delta Air Lines, Garuda Indonesia, Middle East Airlines, and a few unaffiliated carriers.
      </p>
      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_4">
        Terminal 4
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Terminal 4">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Heathrow_LON_04_07_77.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1038" data-file-width="2048" height="112" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Heathrow_LON_04_07_77.JPG/220px-Heathrow_LON_04_07_77.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Heathrow_LON_04_07_77.JPG/330px-Heathrow_LON_04_07_77.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Heathrow_LON_04_07_77.JPG/440px-Heathrow_LON_04_07_77.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Heathrow_LON_04_07_77.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Terminal_4" title="Heathrow Terminal 4">
          Terminal 4
         </a>
         bird's-eye view
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Terminal_4" title="Heathrow Terminal 4">
        Heathrow Terminal 4
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Opened in 1986, Terminal 4 is situated to the south of the southern runway next to the cargo terminal and is connected to Terminals 1, 2 and 3 by the
       <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Cargo_Tunnel" title="Heathrow Cargo Tunnel">
        Heathrow Cargo Tunnel
       </a>
       . The terminal has an area of 105,481 m
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (1,135,390 sq ft) and is now home to the
       <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">
        SkyTeam
       </a>
       alliance, with the exception of
       <a href="/wiki/Garuda_Indonesia" title="Garuda Indonesia">
        Garuda Indonesia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">
        Delta Air Lines
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_East_Airlines" title="Middle East Airlines">
        Middle East Airlines
       </a>
       , which use Terminal 3, Oneworld carriers Malaysia Airlines and Qatar Airways, and to most unaffiliated carriers. It has undergone a £200m upgrade to enable it to accommodate 45 airlines with an upgraded forecourt to reduce traffic congestion and improve security. Most flights that go to Terminal 4 are flights coming from Asia and North Africa, as well as a few flights to Europe. An extended check-in area with renovated piers and departure lounges and a new baggage system were installed, and two new stands were built to accommodate the Airbus A380;
       <a href="/wiki/Etihad_Airways" title="Etihad Airways">
        Etihad Airways
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Malaysia_Airlines" title="Malaysia Airlines">
        Malaysia Airlines
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Airways" title="Qatar Airways">
        Qatar Airways
       </a>
       operate regular A380 flights.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_z_51-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ref_z-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_5">
        Terminal 5
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Terminal 5">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Heathrow_Airport_014.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Heathrow_Airport_014.jpg/220px-Heathrow_Airport_014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Heathrow_Airport_014.jpg/330px-Heathrow_Airport_014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Heathrow_Airport_014.jpg/440px-Heathrow_Airport_014.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Heathrow_Airport_014.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Terminal_5" title="Heathrow Terminal 5">
          Terminal 5
         </a>
         bird's-eye view
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Terminal_5" title="Heathrow Terminal 5">
        Heathrow Terminal 5
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Terminal 5 lies between the northern and southern runways at the western end of the Heathrow site and was opened by Queen Elizabeth II on 14 March 2008,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_2008b_52-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ref_2008b-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       some 19 years after its inception. It opened to the public on 27 March 2008, and British Airways and its partner company Iberia have exclusive use of this terminal. The first passenger to enter Terminal 5 was a UK
       <a href="/wiki/Expatriate" title="Expatriate">
        ex-pat
       </a>
       from Kenya who passed through security at 04:30 on the day. He was presented with a boarding pass by the British Airways CEO Willie Walsh for the first departing flight, BA302 to Paris. During the two weeks after its opening, operations were disrupted by problems with the terminal's IT systems, coupled with insufficient testing and staff training, which caused over 500 flights to be cancelled.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_2008c_53-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ref_2008c-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Until March 2012, Terminal 5 was exclusively used by British Airways as its global hub; however, because of the merger, on 25 March
       <a href="/wiki/Iberia_(airline)" title="Iberia (airline)">
        Iberia's
       </a>
       operations at Heathrow were moved to the terminal, making it the home of
       <a href="/wiki/International_Airlines_Group" title="International Airlines Group">
        International Airlines Group
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Built at a cost of £4.3 billion, the terminal consists of a four-story main terminal building (Concourse A) and two satellite buildings linked to the main terminal by an underground
       <a href="/wiki/People_mover" title="People mover">
        people mover
       </a>
       transit system. The second satellite (Concourse C), includes dedicated aircraft stands for the Airbus A380. It became fully operational on 1 June 2011. Terminal 5 was voted
       <a href="/wiki/Skytrax" title="Skytrax">
        Skytrax
       </a>
       World's Best Airport Terminal 2014 in the Annual World Airport Awards.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The main terminal building (Concourse A) has an area of 300,000 square metres (3,200,000 sq ft) while Concourse B covers 60,000 square metres (650,000 sq ft).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_2011b_56-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ref_2011b-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It has 60 aircraft stands and capacity for 30 million passengers annually as well as more than 100 shops and restaurants.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A further building, designated Concourse D and of similar size to Concourse C, may yet be built to the east of the existing site, providing up to another 16 stands. Following British Airways' merger with
       <a href="/wiki/Iberia_(airline)" title="Iberia (airline)">
        Iberia
       </a>
       , this may become a priority since the combined business will require accommodation at Heathrow under one roof to maximise the cost savings envisaged under the deal. A proposal for Concourse D featured in Heathrow's most recent capital investment plan.
      </p>
      <p>
       The transport network around the airport has been extended to cope with the increase in passenger numbers. A dedicated
       <a href="/wiki/Spur_route" title="Spur route">
        motorway spur
       </a>
       links the terminal to the M25 (between junctions 14 and 15). The terminal has a 3,800 space
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multi-story_car_park" title="Multi-story car park">
        multi-story car park
       </a>
       . A more distant long-stay car park for business passengers is connected to the terminal by a
       <a href="/wiki/Personal_rapid_transit" title="Personal rapid transit">
        personal rapid transit
       </a>
       system, which became operational in the spring of 2011.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       New branches of both the
       <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Express" title="Heathrow Express">
        Heathrow Express
       </a>
       and the Underground's Piccadilly line serve a new shared
       <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Terminal_5_station" title="Heathrow Terminal 5 station">
        Heathrow Terminal 5 station
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_assignments">
        Terminal assignments
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Terminal assignments">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       As of March 2017, Heathrow's four passenger terminals are assigned as follows:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable">
       <tr>
        <th>
         Terminal
        </th>
        <th>
         Airlines and alliances
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <span class="nowrap">
          Terminal 2
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Star_Alliance" title="Star Alliance">
          Star Alliance
         </a>
         , Aer Lingus, Eurowings, Flybe and Icelandair
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         Terminal 3
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Oneworld" title="Oneworld">
          Oneworld
         </a>
         (except Malaysia Airlines, Qatar Airways, Iberia and most British Airways destinations), Delta Air Lines, Garuda Indonesia, Middle East Airlines, Virgin Atlantic and a few non-aligned airlines
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         Terminal 4
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">
          SkyTeam
         </a>
         (except Delta Air Lines, Garuda Indonesia, and Middle East Airlines), Malaysia Airlines, Qatar Airways and most non-aligned airlines
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         Terminal 5
        </td>
        <td>
         British Airways (most destinations, except those at Terminal 3), Iberia and Iberia Express
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       Following the opening of Terminal 5 in March 2008, a hugely complex programme of terminal moves was implemented. This saw many airlines move so as to be grouped in terminals by
       <a href="/wiki/Airline_alliance" title="Airline alliance">
        airline alliance
       </a>
       as far as possible.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_ad_60-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ref_ad-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Following the opening of Phase 1 of the new Terminal 2 in June 2014, all Star Alliance member airlines
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (with the exception of new member Air India which moved in early 2017) along with Aer Lingus and Germanwings relocated to Terminal 2 in a phased process completed on 22 October 2014. Additionally, by 30 June 2015 all airlines left Terminal 1 in preparation for its demolition to make room for the construction of Phase 2 of Terminal 2.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Some other airlines made further minor moves at a later point, e.g. Air India moving from Terminal 4 to the other Star Alliance carriers in Terminal 2
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       or Delta Air Lines merging all departures in Terminal 3 instead of a split between Terminals 3 and 4.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Aer Lingus is expected to move their operations to Terminal 5 along with their IAG partners; British Airways and Iberia in the near future.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Traffic_and_statistics">
        Traffic and statistics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Traffic and statistics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">
        Overview
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Overview">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:London_Heathrow_Statistics.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="865" data-file-width="1402" height="278" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/London_Heathrow_Statistics.png/450px-London_Heathrow_Statistics.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/London_Heathrow_Statistics.png/675px-London_Heathrow_Statistics.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/London_Heathrow_Statistics.png/900px-London_Heathrow_Statistics.png 2x" width="450"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:London_Heathrow_Statistics.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Development of passenger numbers, aircraft movements and air freight between 1986 and 2014
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       When ranked by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" title="World's busiest airports by passenger traffic">
        passenger traffic
       </a>
       , Heathrow is the sixth busiest internationally, behind
       <a href="/wiki/Hartsfield%E2%80%93Jackson_Atlanta_International_Airport" title="Hartsfield–Jackson Atlanta International Airport">
        Hartsfield–Jackson Atlanta International Airport
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Capital_International_Airport" title="Beijing Capital International Airport">
        Beijing Capital International Airport
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Dubai_International_Airport" title="Dubai International Airport">
        Dubai International Airport
       </a>
       , Chicago's
       <a href="/wiki/O%27Hare_International_Airport" title="O'Hare International Airport">
        O'Hare International Airport
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Haneda_Airport" title="Haneda Airport">
        Tokyo Haneda Airport
       </a>
       , for the 12 months ending December 2015.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
        <a href="#cite_note-79">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2015, Heathrow was
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Europe" title="List of the busiest airports in Europe">
        the busiest airport in Europe
       </a>
       in total passenger traffic, with 14% more passengers than
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paris%E2%80%93Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport" title="Paris–Charles de Gaulle Airport">
        Paris–Charles de Gaulle Airport
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cdg_80-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cdg-80">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and 22% more than
       <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Atat%C3%BCrk_Airport" title="Istanbul Atatürk Airport">
        Istanbul Atatürk Airport
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
        <a href="#cite_note-81">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Heathrow was the fourth busiest European airport by cargo traffic in 2013, after
       <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">
        Frankfurt Airport
       </a>
       , Paris Charles de Gaulle and
       <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol" title="Amsterdam Airport Schiphol">
        Amsterdam Airport Schiphol
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Busiest_routes">
        Busiest routes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Busiest routes">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Heathrow Airport processed 75,711,130 passengers in 2016.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stats_1-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-stats-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">
        New York's John F. Kennedy International Airport
       </a>
       was the most popular route with 2,934,554 passengers. Including
       <a href="/wiki/Newark_Liberty_International_Airport" title="Newark Liberty International Airport">
        Newark Liberty International Airport
       </a>
       , there are about 4,000,000 passengers going to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Metropolitan_Area" title="New York Metropolitan Area">
        New York Metropolitan Area
       </a>
       annually.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-routestats_84-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-routestats-84">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The table below shows the 40 busiest routes at the airport in 2016.
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable sortable" style="font-size: 87.5%">

         </sup>
        </b>

         </a>
        </td>

         702,842
        </td>
