      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_facilities">
        Other facilities
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Other facilities">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Compass_Building_on_the_Bath_Road_by_Philip_Jeffrey.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1065" data-file-width="1600" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Compass_Building_on_the_Bath_Road_by_Philip_Jeffrey.jpg/220px-Compass_Building_on_the_Bath_Road_by_Philip_Jeffrey.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Compass_Building_on_the_Bath_Road_by_Philip_Jeffrey.jpg/330px-Compass_Building_on_the_Bath_Road_by_Philip_Jeffrey.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Compass_Building_on_the_Bath_Road_by_Philip_Jeffrey.jpg/440px-Compass_Building_on_the_Bath_Road_by_Philip_Jeffrey.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Compass_Building_on_the_Bath_Road_by_Philip_Jeffrey.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Compass_Centre" title="Compass Centre">
          Compass Centre
         </a>
         , the head office of Heathrow Airport Holdings
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The head office of
       <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport_Holdings" title="Heathrow Airport Holdings">
        Heathrow Airport Holdings
       </a>
       (formerly BAA Limited) is located in the
       <a href="/wiki/Compass_Centre" title="Compass Centre">
        Compass Centre
       </a>
       by Heathrow's northern runway, a building that previously served as a British Airways flight crew centre.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_ag_85-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ref_ag-85">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The World Business Centre Heathrow consists of buildings one and two. 1 World Business Centre houses offices of Heathrow Airport Holdings, Heathrow Airport itself, and
       <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Airlines" title="Scandinavian Airlines">
        Scandinavian Airlines
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Previously
       <a href="/wiki/International_Airlines_Group" title="International Airlines Group">
        International Airlines Group
       </a>
       had its head office in 2 World Business Centre.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
        <a href="#cite_note-87">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       At one time the British Airways head office was located within Heathrow Airport at Speedbird House
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_ah_89-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ref_ah-89">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       before the completion of
       <a href="/wiki/Waterside_(building)" title="Waterside (building)">
        Waterside
       </a>
       , the current BA head office in
       <a href="/wiki/Harmondsworth" title="Harmondsworth">
        Harmondsworth
       </a>
       , in June 1998.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McKellar200_90-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-McKellar200-90">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       To the north of the airfield lies the Northern Perimeter Road, along which most of Heathrow's car rental agencies are based, and Bath Road, which runs parallel to it, but outside the airport campus–this is nicknamed "The Strip" by locals owing to its continuous line of airport hotels.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Access">
        Access
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Access">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transport">
        Public transport
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Public transport">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Train">
        Train
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Train">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:332002_at_Paddington_ABU.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="532" data-file-width="800" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/332002_at_Paddington_ABU.jpg/220px-332002_at_Paddington_ABU.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/332002_at_Paddington_ABU.jpg/330px-332002_at_Paddington_ABU.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/332002_at_Paddington_ABU.jpg/440px-332002_at_Paddington_ABU.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:332002_at_Paddington_ABU.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Express" title="Heathrow Express">
          Heathrow Express
         </a>
         train at
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paddington_station" title="Paddington station">
          Paddington station
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Express" title="Heathrow Express">
         Heathrow Express
        </a>
        : a non-stop service direct to London's
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paddington_station" title="Paddington station">
         Paddington station
        </a>
        ; trains leave every 15 minutes for the 15-minute journey (21 minutes to/from Terminal 5). Trains depart from
        <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Terminal_5_station" title="Heathrow Terminal 5 station">
         Heathrow Terminal 5 station
        </a>
        or
        <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Central_railway_station" title="Heathrow Central railway station">
         Heathrow Central station
        </a>
        (Terminals 2 &amp; 3). A Heathrow Express transfer service operates between Terminal 4 and Heathrow Central to connect with services from London and Terminal 5.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Connect" title="Heathrow Connect">
         Heathrow Connect
        </a>
        : a stopping service to Paddington calling at up to five
        <a href="/wiki/National_Rail" title="National Rail">
         National Rail
        </a>
        stations en route – trains leave every 30 minutes for the 27-minute journey.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
         <a href="#cite_note-91">
          [89]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Heathrow Connect services terminate at Heathrow Central station. Calls at
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hayes_and_Harlington_railway_station" title="Hayes and Harlington railway station">
         Hayes and Harlington
        </a>
        for connecting trains to
        <a href="/wiki/Reading_railway_station" title="Reading railway station">
         Reading
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">
         London Underground
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Piccadilly_line" title="Piccadilly line">
         Piccadilly line
        </a>
        ): four stations serve the airport:
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heathrow_Terminals_1,_2,_3_tube_station" title="Heathrow Terminals 1, 2, 3 tube station">
         Terminal 2 and 3
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Terminal_4_tube_station" title="Heathrow Terminal 4 tube station">
         Terminal 4
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Terminal_5_station" title="Heathrow Terminal 5 station">
         Terminal 5
        </a>
        serve the passenger terminals; and
        <a href="/wiki/Hatton_Cross_tube_station" title="Hatton Cross tube station">
         Hatton Cross
        </a>
        the maintenance areas. The usual journey time from Heathrow Central to Central London is around 40–50 minutes.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
         <a href="#cite_note-92">
          [90]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Bus_and_coach">
        Bus and coach
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Bus and coach">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Many buses and coaches operate from the large
       <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Central_bus_station" title="Heathrow Central bus station">
        Heathrow Central bus station
       </a>
       serving Terminals 2 and 3, and also from bus stations at Terminals 4 and 5.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Inter-terminal_transport">
        Inter-terminal transport
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Inter-terminal transport">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Terminals 2 and 3 are within walking distance of each other. Transfers to Terminal 4 and 5 are by
       <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Express" title="Heathrow Express">
        Heathrow Express
       </a>
       trains or bus. Heathrow Express and Heathrow Connect train services between Heathrow Central and Terminals 4 and 5 are free of charge.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This is also true for London Underground services when using an Oyster card. When travelling to Terminal 4, one has to change at
       <a href="/wiki/Hatton_Cross_tube_station" title="Hatton Cross tube station">
        Hatton Cross
       </a>
       , whilst this station not being part of the actual free fare zone. Local buses throughout the airport area are provided free of charge under the "Heathrow FreeFlow" scheme;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
        <a href="#cite_note-94">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
       passengers should tell the driver their destination to ensure they are not charged a fare.
      </p>
      <p>
       Transit passengers remaining
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Airside_(airport)" title="Airside (airport)">
        airside
       </a>
       are provided with free dedicated transfer buses between terminals.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ULTra" title="ULTra">
        ULTra Personal Rapid Transport
       </a>
       opened in April 2011 to shuttle passengers between Terminal 5 and the business car park at a speed of up to 40 km/h (25 mph). There are 21 small transportation pods that can each carry up to four adults, two children, and their luggage. The pods are battery-powered and run on a four-kilometre track. The capsules run on demand. The provider claims a 95% availability rate and no accidents so far.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_2009c_95-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ref_2009c-95">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Plans to use the same technology to connect Terminals 2 and 3 to remote car parks were included in the draft 2014–2019 five-year master plan but have since been deferred due to other priorities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Taxi">
        Taxi
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Taxi">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Taxis are available at all terminals.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
        <a href="#cite_note-97">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Car">
        Car
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Car">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Heathrow_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_231165.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Heathrow_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_231165.jpg/220px-Heathrow_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_231165.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Heathrow_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_231165.jpg/330px-Heathrow_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_231165.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Heathrow_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_231165.jpg/440px-Heathrow_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_231165.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Heathrow_Airport_-_geograph.org.uk_-_231165.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Entrance at the southern end of the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M4_Motorway" title="M4 Motorway">
          M4 Motorway
         </a>
         spur, showing a scale model of Concorde, replaced since 2008 by the Emirates A380 scale model.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
          <a href="#cite_note-98">
           [96]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Heathrow is accessible via the nearby
       <a href="/wiki/M4_motorway" title="M4 motorway">
        M4 motorway
       </a>
       or
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A4_road_(Great_Britain)" title="A4 road (Great Britain)">
        A4 road
       </a>
       (Terminals 2–3), the
       <a href="/wiki/M25_motorway" title="M25 motorway">
        M25 motorway
       </a>
       (Terminals 4 and 5) and the
       <a href="/wiki/A30_road" title="A30 road">
        A30 road
       </a>
       (Terminal 4). There are drop-off and pick-up areas at all terminals and short-
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
        <a href="#cite_note-99">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and long-stay
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
        <a href="#cite_note-100">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
       multi-storey car parks. All the Heathrow forecourts are drop-off only.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_101-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-101">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are further car parks, not run by Heathrow Airport Holdings, just outside the airport: the most recognisable is the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Car_Parks" title="National Car Parks">
        National Car Parks
       </a>
       facility, although there are many other options; these car parks are connected to the terminals by shuttle buses.
      </p>
      <p>
       Four parallel tunnels under the northern runway connect the M4 Heathrow spur and the A4 road to Terminals 2–3. The two larger tunnels are each two lanes wide and are used for motorised traffic. The two smaller tunnels were originally reserved for pedestrians and bicycles; to increase traffic capacity the cycle lanes have been modified to each take a single lane of cars, although bicycles still have priority over cars. Pedestrian access to the smaller tunnels has been discontinued, with the free bus services being used instead.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Bicycle">
        Bicycle
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Bicycle">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       There are (mainly off-road) bicycle routes to some of the terminals.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_aq_102-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ref_aq-102">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Free bicycle parking places are available in car parks 1 and 1A, at Terminal 4, and to the North and South of Terminal 5's Interchange Plaza. It is worth noting you are not allowed to cycle through the main tunnel to access Terminals 2 and 3 (Terminal 1 closed in 2015).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_ar_103-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ref_ar-103">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Incidents_and_accidents">
        Incidents and accidents
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Incidents and accidents">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <ul>
       <li>
        On 3 March 1948, Sabena
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Douglas_DC3" title="Douglas DC3">
         Douglas DC3
        </a>
        OO-AWH crashed in fog. Three crew and 19 of the 22 passengers on board died.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_2003_104-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Ref_2003-104">
          [102]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        On 31 October 1950,
        <a href="/wiki/British_European_Airways" title="British European Airways">
         BEA
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Vickers_VC.1_Viking" title="Vickers VC.1 Viking">
         Vickers Viking
        </a>
        G-AHPN crashed at Heathrow after hitting the runway during a go-around. Three crew and 25 passengers died.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_as_105-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Ref_as-105">
          [103]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        On 16 January 1955,
        <a href="/wiki/British_European_Airways" title="British European Airways">
         BEA
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Viscount" title="Vickers Viscount">
         Vickers Viscount
        </a>
        G-AMOK crashed into barriers whilst taking off in fog from a disused runway strip parallel to the desired runway. There were 2 injuries.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kazakhstan_Government_106-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Kazakhstan_Government-106">
          [104]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        On 22 June 1955,
        <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Airways_Corporation" title="British Overseas Airways Corporation">
         BOAC
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Dove" title="De Havilland Dove">
         de Havilland Dove
        </a>
        G-ALTM crashed just short of the runway during a filming flight, when the pilot shut-down the incorrect engine. There were no casualties.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Flight_Global_107-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Flight_Global-107">
          [105]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        On 1 October 1956, XA897, an
        <a href="/wiki/Avro_Vulcan" title="Avro Vulcan">
         Avro Vulcan
        </a>
        strategic bomber of the
        <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">
         Royal Air Force
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/1956_London_Heathrow_Avro_Vulcan_crash" title="1956 London Heathrow Avro Vulcan crash">
         crashed at Heathrow
        </a>
        after an approach in bad weather. The Vulcan was the first to be delivered to the RAF, and was returning from a demonstration flight to Australia and New Zealand. The pilot and co-pilot ejected and survived, but the four other occupants were killed.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Blackman142_108-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Blackman142-108">
          [106]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        On 7 January 1960, Vickers Viscount G-AOHU of BEA was damaged beyond economic repair when the nose wheel collapsed on landing. A fire then developed and burnt out the fuselage. There were no casualties among the 59 people on board.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ASN070160_109-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-ASN070160-109">
          [107]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        On 27 October 1965, BEA
        <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Vanguard" title="Vickers Vanguard">
         Vickers Vanguard
        </a>
        G-APEE, flying from Edinburgh, crashed on Runway 28R while attempting to land in poor visibility. All 30 passengers and six crew on board died.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_at_110-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Ref_at-110">
          [108]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Scotsman_111-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Scotsman-111">
          [109]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        On 8 April 1968,
        <a href="/wiki/BOAC_Flight_712" title="BOAC Flight 712">
         BOAC Flight 712
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Boeing_707" title="Boeing 707">
         Boeing 707
        </a>
        G-ARWE, departing for Australia via Singapore, suffered an engine fire just after take-off. The engine fell from the wing into a nearby gravel pit in
        <a href="/wiki/Staines-upon-Thames" title="Staines-upon-Thames">
         Staines
        </a>
        , before the plane managed to perform an emergency landing with the wing on fire. However, the plane was consumed by fire once on the ground. Five people – four passengers and a stewardess – died, while 122 survived.
        <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Jane_Harrison" title="Barbara Jane Harrison">
         Barbara Harrison
        </a>
        , a flight attendant on board who helped with the evacuation, was posthumously awarded the
        <a href="/wiki/George_Cross" title="George Cross">
         George Cross
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_av_112-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Ref_av-112">
          [110]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        On 3 July 1968, the port flap operating rod of
        <a href="/wiki/1968_Heathrow_BKS_Air_Transport_Airspeed_Ambassador_crash" title="1968 Heathrow BKS Air Transport Airspeed Ambassador crash">
         G-AMAD
        </a>
        , an
        <a href="/wiki/Airspeed_Ambassador" title="Airspeed Ambassador">
         Airspeed Ambassador
        </a>
        operated by BKS Air Transport failed due to fatigue thereby allowing the port flaps to retract. This resulted in a rolling movement to port which could not be controlled during the approach, causing the aircraft to contact the grass and swerve towards the terminal building. It hit two parked British European Airways
        <a href="/wiki/Hawker_Siddeley_Trident" title="Hawker Siddeley Trident">
         Hawker Siddeley Trident
        </a>
        aircraft, burst into flames and came to rest against the ground floor of the terminal building. Six of the eight crew died, as did eight horses on board. Trident G-ARPT was written off,
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_aw_113-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Ref_aw-113">
          [111]
         </a>
        </sup>
        and Trident G-ARPI was badly damaged, but subsequently repaired, only to be lost in the Staines crash in 1972.
       </li>
       <li>
        On 22 January 1970, Vickers Viscount G-AWXI of British Midland was damaged beyond economic repair when an engine caught fire on take-off. A successful emergency landing was made at Heathrow.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ASN22011970_114-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-ASN22011970-114">
          [112]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        On 18 June 1972, Trident G-ARPI, operating as
        <a href="/wiki/British_European_Airways_Flight_548" title="British European Airways Flight 548">
         BEA548
        </a>
        , crashed in a field close to the Crooked Billet Public House, Staines, two minutes after taking off. All 118 passengers and crew on board died.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
         <a href="#cite_note-115">
          [113]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BA38_Crash.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2896" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/BA38_Crash.jpg/220px-BA38_Crash.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/BA38_Crash.jpg/330px-BA38_Crash.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/BA38_Crash.jpg/440px-BA38_Crash.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BA38_Crash.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/British_Airways_Flight_38" title="British Airways Flight 38">
          British Airways Flight 38
         </a>
         which crash landed just short of the runway on 17 January 2008
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <ul>
       <li>
        On 8 December 1996, a
        <a href="/wiki/KLM_Cityhopper" title="KLM Cityhopper">
         KLM Cityhopper
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Fokker_50" title="Fokker 50">
         Fokker 50
        </a>
        , PH-KVK, operating as KLM483 from Rotterdam, suffered a main gear collapse after landing on runway 09R. The aircraft's touchdown was normal, right mainwheel first. About 5 seconds after all the landing gear were in ground contact the left main landing gear collapsed and the aircraft left wing tip, left propeller and the rear left portion of the fuselage contacted the runway. The aircraft veered to the left coming to rest on the hard surface clear of the runway in Block 81.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
         <a href="#cite_note-116">
          [114]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
         <a href="#cite_note-117">
          [115]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        On 5 November 1997, a Virgin Atlantic
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Airbus_A340-300" title="Airbus A340-300">
         Airbus A340-300
        </a>
        , G-VSKY, made an emergency landing following an undercarriage malfunction. Part of the undercarriage collapsed on landing, and both aircraft and runway were damaged. Recommendations made as a result of the accident included one that aircraft cabin door simulators should more accurately reproduce operating characteristics in an emergency, and another that
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cockpit_voice_recorder" title="Cockpit voice recorder">
         cockpit voice recorders
        </a>
        should have a two-hour duration in aircraft registered before April 1998.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
         <a href="#cite_note-118">
          [116]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        On 17 January 2008, a British Airways
        <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777" title="Boeing 777">
         Boeing 777-236ER
        </a>
        , G-YMMM, operating
        <a href="/wiki/British_Airways_Flight_38" title="British Airways Flight 38">
         flight BA038
        </a>
        from Beijing, crash-landed at Heathrow. The aircraft landed on grass short of the south runway, then slid to the edge of the runway and stopped on the threshold, leading to eighteen minor injuries. The aircraft was later found to have suffered loss of thrust caused by fuel icing.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
         <a href="#cite_note-119">
          [117]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Terrorism_and_security_incidents">
        Terrorism and security incidents
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Terrorism and security incidents">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        On 8 June 1968,
        <a href="/wiki/James_Earl_Ray" title="James Earl Ray">
         James Earl Ray
        </a>
        , the man convicted of the assassination of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King,_Jr." title="Martin Luther King, Jr.">
         Martin Luther King, Jr.
        </a>
        , was captured and arrested at Heathrow Airport while attempting to leave the United Kingdom on a false Canadian passport.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Borrell1968_120-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Borrell1968-120">
          [118]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        On 6 September 1970,
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_Al_Flight_219" title="El Al Flight 219">
         El Al Flight 219
        </a>
        experienced an attempted hijack by two
        <a href="/wiki/Popular_Front_for_the_Liberation_of_Palestine" title="Popular Front for the Liberation of Palestine">
         PFLP
        </a>
        members. One hijacker was killed and the other was subdued as the plane made an emergency landing at Heathrow Airport.
       </li>
       <li>
        On 19 May 1974, the
        <a href="/wiki/Provisional_Irish_Republican_Army" title="Provisional Irish Republican Army">
         IRA
        </a>
        planted a series of bombs in the Terminal 1 car park. Two people were injured by the explosions.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_ax_121-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Ref_ax-121">
          [119]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        On 26 November 1983, the
        <a href="/wiki/Brink%27s-Mat_robbery" title="Brink's-Mat robbery">
         Brink's-Mat robbery
        </a>
        occurred, in which 6,800 gold bars worth nearly £26 million were taken from a vault near Heathrow. Only a small amount of the gold was recovered, and only two men were convicted of the crime.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_2000_122-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Ref_2000-122">
          [120]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        On 17 April 1986,
        <a href="/wiki/Semtex" title="Semtex">
         semtex
        </a>
        explosives were found in the bag of a pregnant Irishwoman attempting to board an
        <a href="/wiki/El_Al" title="El Al">
         El Al
        </a>
        flight. The explosives had been given to her by her Jordanian boyfriend and father of her unborn child
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nizar_Hindawi" title="Nizar Hindawi">
         Nizar Hindawi
        </a>
        . The incident became known as the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindawi_Affair" title="Hindawi Affair">
         Hindawi Affair
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reynolds2002_123-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Reynolds2002-123">
          [121]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        On 21 December 1988,
        <a href="/wiki/Pan_Am_Flight_103" title="Pan Am Flight 103">
         Pan Am Flight 103
        </a>
        from Heathrow to New York/JFK was blown up over Lockerbie, Scotland, killing all 259 on board and 11 other people on the ground. This also still remains the deadliest attack on a US aircraft.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
         <a href="#cite_note-124">
          [122]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        In 1994, over a six-day period, Heathrow was targeted three times (8, 10, and 13 March) by the
        <a href="/wiki/Provisional_Irish_Republican_Army" title="Provisional Irish Republican Army">
         IRA
        </a>
        , which fired 12 mortars. Heathrow was a symbolic target due to its importance to the UK economy, and much disruption was caused when areas of the airport were closed over the period. The gravity of the incident was heightened by the fact that the Queen was being flown back to Heathrow by the RAF on 10 March.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Henderson1998_125-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Henderson1998-125">
          [123]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        In March 2002, thieves stole US$3 million that had arrived on a
        <a href="/wiki/South_African_Airways" title="South African Airways">
         South African Airways
        </a>
        flight.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_2002a_126-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Ref_2002a-126">
          [124]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        In February 2003, the
        <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">
         British Army
        </a>
        was deployed to Heathrow along with 1,000 police officers in response to intelligence reports suggesting that
        <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">
         al-Qaeda
        </a>
        terrorists might launch
        <a href="/wiki/Surface-to-air_missile" title="Surface-to-air missile">
         surface-to-air missile
        </a>
        attacks at British or American airliners.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_ay_127-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Ref_ay-127">
          [125]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        On 17 May 2004, Scotland Yard's
        <a href="/wiki/Flying_Squad" title="Flying Squad">
         Flying Squad
        </a>
        foiled an attempt by seven men to steal £40 million in gold bullion and a similar quantity of cash from the
        <a href="/wiki/Swissport" title="Swissport">
         Swissport
        </a>
        warehouse at Heathrow.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_az_128-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Ref_az-128">
          [126]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        On 10 August 2006, the airport became the focus of changes in security protocol, following the revelation of a supposed al-Qaeda
        <a href="/wiki/2006_transatlantic_aircraft_plot" title="2006 transatlantic aircraft plot">
         terrorist plot
        </a>
        . New security rules were put in force immediately, causing additional restrictions in regards to carrying liquids onto flights. This caused longer queues and wait times at security. These included the prohibition of carry-on luggage (except essential items such as travel documents and medication) and all liquids – although this rule was later relaxed to allow the carrying on board of liquid medications and baby milk, if they were tasted first by passengers at the security checkpoint.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">
         <a href="#cite_note-129">
          [127]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        On 25 February 2008,
        <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace" title="Greenpeace">
         Greenpeace
        </a>
        activists protesting against the planned third runway managed to cross the tarmac and climb atop a British Airways
        <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320_family" title="Airbus A320 family">
         Airbus A320
        </a>
        , which had just arrived from
        <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">
         Manchester Airport
        </a>
        . At about 09:45 GMT the protesters unveiled a banner, saying "Climate Emergency – No Third Runway", over the aircraft's
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vertical_stabiliser" title="Vertical stabiliser">
         tailfin
        </a>
        . By 11:00 GMT four arrests had been made.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_2008e_130-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Ref_2008e-130">
          [128]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        On 13 March 2008, a man with a rucksack scaled the perimeter fence onto runway 27R, and ran across the grounds, resulting in his subsequent arrest. A controlled explosion of his bag took place, although nothing suspicious was found, and the
        <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Police_Service" title="Metropolitan Police Service">
         Metropolitan Police
        </a>
        later said that the incident had not been terrorism related.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_2008f_131-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Ref_2008f-131">
          [129]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        On 13 July 2015, thirteen activists belonging to the climate change protest group
        <a href="/wiki/Plane_Stupid" title="Plane Stupid">
         Plane Stupid
        </a>
        managed to break through the perimeter fence and get onto the northern runway. They chained themselves together in protest, disrupting hundreds of flights. All were eventually arrested.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">
         <a href="#cite_note-132">
          [130]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">
         <a href="#cite_note-133">
          [131]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_incidents">
        Other incidents
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Other incidents">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Flights from Heathrow were suspended from midday Thursday 15 April 2010 to 22:00 Tuesday 20 April 2010 due to risk of jet engines being
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jet_engines_and_volcanic_ash" title="Jet engines and volcanic ash">
         damaged by volcanic ash
        </a>
        in the upper atmosphere caused by the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010_eruption_of_Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull" title="2010 eruption of Eyjafjallajökull">
         eruption of Eyjafjallajökull
        </a>
        in Iceland.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_aba_134-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Ref_aba-134">
          [132]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        On 18 December 2010, 'heavy' (9 cm, according to the Heathrow Winter Resilience Enquiry)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">
         <a href="#cite_note-135">
          [133]
         </a>
        </sup>
        snowfall caused the closure of the entire airport, causing one of the largest incidents at Heathrow of all time. 4,000 flights were cancelled over five days and 9,500 passengers spent the night at Heathrow on 18 December following the initial snowfall.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">
         <a href="#cite_note-136">
          [134]
         </a>
        </sup>
        The problems were caused not only by snow on the runways, but also by snow and ice on the 198 parking stands which were all occupied by aircraft.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
         <a href="#cite_note-137">
          [135]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        On 12 July 2013, an
        <a href="/wiki/Ethiopian_Airlines" title="Ethiopian Airlines">
         Ethiopian Airlines
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787_Dreamliner" title="Boeing 787 Dreamliner">
         Boeing 787 Dreamliner
        </a>
        parked at Heathrow airport caught fire.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">
         <a href="#cite_note-138">
          [136]
         </a>
        </sup>
        There were no passengers aboard and no injuries. The cause is under investigation.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">
         <a href="#cite_note-139">
          [137]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Future_expansion_and_plans">
        Future expansion and plans
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Future expansion and plans">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Runway_and_terminal_expansion">
        Runway and terminal expansion
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Runway and terminal expansion">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Expansion_of_Heathrow_Airport" title="Expansion of Heathrow Airport">
        Expansion of Heathrow Airport
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Take_off_queue,_Heathrow,_10_Sept._2010_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1926" data-file-width="3362" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Take_off_queue%2C_Heathrow%2C_10_Sept._2010_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg/220px-Take_off_queue%2C_Heathrow%2C_10_Sept._2010_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Take_off_queue%2C_Heathrow%2C_10_Sept._2010_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg/330px-Take_off_queue%2C_Heathrow%2C_10_Sept._2010_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Take_off_queue%2C_Heathrow%2C_10_Sept._2010_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg/440px-Take_off_queue%2C_Heathrow%2C_10_Sept._2010_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Take_off_queue,_Heathrow,_10_Sept._2010_-_Flickr_-_PhillipC.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         British Airways aircraft queuing for take-off
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In January 2009, the Transport Secretary at the time,
       <a href="/wiki/Geoff_Hoon" title="Geoff Hoon">
        Geoff Hoon
       </a>
       announced that the
       <a href="/wiki/Brown_ministry" title="Brown ministry">
        British government
       </a>
       supported the expansion of Heathrow by building a third 2,200-metre (7,200 ft) runway and a sixth terminal building.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_abb_140-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ref_abb-140">
         [138]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This decision followed the 2003 white paper on the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_transport_and_the_environment_(United_Kingdom)#Airport_development_strategy" title="Air transport and the environment (United Kingdom)">
        future of air transport in the UK
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_2003a_141-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ref_2003a-141">
         [139]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and a public consultation in November 2007.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_2007a_142-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ref_2007a-142">
         [140]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This was a controversial decision which met with widespread opposition because of the expected greenhouse gas emissions, impact on local communities, as well as noise and air pollution concerns.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">
        <a href="#cite_note-143">
         [141]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Prior to the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2010" title="United Kingdom general election, 2010">
        2010 general election
       </a>
       , the Conservative and Liberal Democrat parties announced that they would prevent the construction of any third runway or further material expansion of the airport's operating capacity. The Mayor of London, then
       <a href="/wiki/Boris_Johnson" title="Boris Johnson">
        Boris Johnson
       </a>
       , took the position that London needs more airport capacity, favouring the construction of an entirely
       <a href="/wiki/Thames_Estuary_Airport" title="Thames Estuary Airport">
        new airport
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Thames_Estuary" title="Thames Estuary">
        Thames Estuary
       </a>
       rather than expanding Heathrow.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_abe_144-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ref_abe-144">
         [142]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After the Conservative-Liberal Democrat coalition took power, it was announced that the third runway expansion was cancelled.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cancelled_145-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Cancelled-145">
         [143]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Two years later, leading Conservatives were reported to have changed their minds on the subject.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PossibleUTurn_146-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-PossibleUTurn-146">
         [144]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Another proposal for expanding Heathrow's capacity was the
       <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Hub" title="Heathrow Hub">
        Heathrow Hub
       </a>
       , which aims to extend both runways to a total length of about 7,000 metres and divide them into four so that they each provide two, full length runways, allowing simultaneous take-offs and landings while decreasing noise levels.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">
        <a href="#cite_note-147">
         [145]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CPS_paper_148-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CPS_paper-148">
         [146]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In July 2013, the airport submitted three new proposals for expansion to the Airports Commission, which was established to review airport capacity in the southeast of England. The Airports Commission was chaired by Sir Howard Davies who, at the time of his appointment was in the employ of GIC Private Limited (formerly known as Government Investment Corporation of Singapore) and a member of its International Advisory Board. GIC Private Limited was then (2012), as it remains today, one of Heathrow's principal owners. Sir Howard Davies resigned these positions upon confirmation of his appointment to lead the Airports Commission, although it has been observed that he failed to identify these interests when invited to complete the Airports Commission's register of interests. Each of the three proposals that were to be considered by Sir Howard Davies's commission involved the construction of a third runway, either to the north, northwest or southwest of the airport.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149">
        <a href="#cite_note-149">
         [147]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The commission released its interim report in December 2013, shortlisting three options: the north-west third runway option at Heathrow, extending an existing runway at Heathrow, and a second runway at
       <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">
        Gatwick Airport
       </a>
       . After this report was published, the government confirmed that no options had been ruled out for airport expansion in the South-east and that a new runway would not be built at Heathrow before 2015.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC-shortlist_150-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-BBC-shortlist-150">
         [148]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The full report was published on 1 July 2015, and backed a third, north-west, runway at Heathrow.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151">
        <a href="#cite_note-151">
         [149]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Reaction to the report was generally negative, particularly from London Mayor Boris Johnson. One senior Conservative told
       <a href="/wiki/Channel_4" title="Channel 4">
        Channel 4
       </a>
       : "Howard Davies has dumped an utter steaming pile of poo on the Prime Minister's desk."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152">
        <a href="#cite_note-152">
         [150]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On 25 October 2016, the government confirmed that Heathrow would be allowed to build a third runway; however a final decision would not be taken until winter of 2017/18, after consultations and government votes. The earliest opening year would be 2025.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Heathrow_railway_hub">
        Heathrow railway hub
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Heathrow railway hub">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       A plan to make Heathrow an international railway exchange has also been proposed with the potential construction of
       <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Hub_railway_station" title="Heathrow Hub railway station">
        Heathrow Hub railway station
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oakeshott2009_153-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Oakeshott2009-153">
         [151]
        </a>
       </sup>
       built on a link to the
       <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_2" title="High Speed 2">
        High Speed 2
       </a>
       (HS2) railway line.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154">
        <a href="#cite_note-154">
         [152]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This plan was confirmed to be outside the plans for both Phase 1 &amp; Phase 2 of the plans for HS2 in March 2015.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155">
        <a href="#cite_note-155">
         [153]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Airtrack">
        Airtrack
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Airtrack">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In July 2009, Heathrow Airport Limited submitted an application to the Secretary of State for Transport seeking to gain authorisation to develop a new rail link to Heathrow Terminal 5 to be known as
       <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airtrack" title="Heathrow Airtrack">
        Heathrow Airtrack
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156">
        <a href="#cite_note-156">
         [154]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The rail link would address the current lack of public transport available to the South West of the Airport by connecting to Guildford, Reading and London Waterloo. BAA stated that the scheme should add significantly to its aim of increasing the proportion of people using public transport to travel to the airport.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ref_abd_157-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ref_abd-157">
         [155]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In April 2011, BAA announced that it was abandoning the project,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">
        <a href="#cite_note-158">
         [156]
        </a>
       </sup>
       citing the unavailability of government subsidy and other priorities for Heathrow,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">
        <a href="#cite_note-159">
         [157]
        </a>
       </sup>
       such as linking to
       <a href="/wiki/Crossrail" title="Crossrail">
        Crossrail
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HS2" title="HS2">
        HS2
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Heathrow.2FGatwick_rail_link">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Heathrow/Gatwick_rail_link">
        Heathrow/Gatwick rail link
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Heathrow/Gatwick rail link">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Heathwick" title="Heathwick">
        Heathwick
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       In late 2011, the
       <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Transport" title="Department for Transport">
        Department for Transport
       </a>
       began studying the feasibility of a high-speed rail link between Gatwick and Heathrow Airport. This rail link would form part of a plan to combine the UK's two biggest airports into a "collective" or "virtual hub" dubbed
       <i>
        Heathwick
       </i>
       . The scheme envisages a 35-mile (56 km) high-speed rail route linking the two airports in fifteen minutes, with trains travelling at a top speed of 180 miles per hour (290 km/h) parallel to the
       <a href="/wiki/M25_motorway" title="M25 motorway">
        M25
       </a>
       and passengers passing through immigration or check-in only once.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160">
        <a href="#cite_note-160">
         [158]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Heathrow_City">
        Heathrow City
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Heathrow_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Heathrow City">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_London" title="Mayor of London">
        Mayor of London
       </a>
       's office and
       <a href="/wiki/Transport_for_London" title="Transport for London">
        Transport for London
       </a>
       commissioned plans in the event of Heathrow's closure—to replace it by a large built-up area.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161">
        <a href="#cite_note-161">
         [159]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162">
        <a href="#cite_note-162">
         [160]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163">
        <a href="#cite_note-163">
         [161]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164">
        <a href="#cite_note-164">
         [162]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some of the plans seem to show terminal 5, or part of it, kept as a shopping centre.
      </p>
